FOREWORD
Our data recorded in this volume is from one of the Mun dialects spoken in
Funing MV- county, Yunnan SP^j province, China. Another Mun dialect was
( ) ( )
M H
further recorded earlier by ourselves in Hainan Island ( P§ ) and its data was
published in 1990 (Tadahiko L. A. Shintani, Yang Zhao, The Mun Language ofHainan
Island, ILCAA, Tokyo). Our Funing field data seems to be worth publishing in the
sense that it can help further comprehensive study of the historical phonology of both
the Mun language itself and the extended Miao-Yao language family to which the Mun
language belongs.
The Mun language data of this lexicon was collected in Funing county
according to our last publication, of which the arrangement of the items was principally
based on theHandbook ofChinese Dialect Vocabulary f^JafslftPS^ffflJ published at the
Princeton University in 1972.
Our survey in Funing county has successfully achieved its purpose thanks to
many Mun collaborators in the field to whom we are very grateful. Our Mun language
data was supplied principally by two native speakers, namely Mr. Zhou Zhenghua ( joj
iEip ) and Ms. Zhao Meilian ( SS^3E ) to whom we are deeply indebted. We are
indebted to the Japan Society for the Promotion of Science who financed our field
research in Funing under the grant-in-aid for international scientific research program.
Tokyo, January 30th, 2008
The Author
INTRODUCTION
Structure of Mun syllable
The syllable ofthe Mun language can be schematized as follow
:
CiV(C T
2)/
( Ci = initial consonant including consonant cluster, V = vowel including
vowel cluster, C 2 = final consonant, T = tone )
Initial consonants
m w
p b
pj bj mj
pi bl
t d n s 1
ts dz e a
n
k g
tj
kj gj
kl gl
kw gw
rjw
9
/ts/, /dz/, /s/ are often palatalized when they are followed by the vowel /i/.
Although we mentioned in our last publication that the tripartite initial oppositon
(voiceless unaspirated / voiceless aspirated / voiced) had been transphonologized to the
tonal opposition in the Mun language, in fact, we found a lot of exceptions with initial
voiceless aspirated consonants in Hainan island, most of which are Chinese loans. The
Funing dialect, on the other hand, has no aspirated consonants even among the Chinese
loans with only one exception bjao53 ts'a53 "fishing fork" (026021).
:
Since we can observe that / G / of Funing dialect corresponds regulary to HI ofHainan
dialect, we can trace the evolution like *s >0> t, which is similar to what happened
in Vietnamese.

Tones
There are seven tonemes
:
open closedsyllable closedsyllable with long
syllable with short vowel vowelor vowel cluster
(1) 13 13
(2) 53 53
(3) 22 22
(4) 35
(5) 354
(6) 44 44
(7) 31 31
This is a case of tripartition of tonal system according to the nature of the initial
consonants ofthe Miao-Yao common, and the schema of its evolution is as follows :

Chinese loan words
A certain number of syllables which seem to have been borrowed from Chinese,
correspond to two or three different syllables in the Funing dialect ofthe Mun language.
Such phenomenon may suggest a possibility of different historical stages of linguistic
contact between the Mun and the Chinese peoples, but we cannot say much about this
matter at the present level ofour knowledge. We just enumerate here certain number of
xiii
such examples
:
